text:
A little addition to the timing debate--I still have my mother's recipe from 30 years ago and it stresses that you need to bring this recipe to a ROLLING BOIL and then time your minute. If you begin timing when the recipe "just boils" you won't get the same texture or set.  Once you hit a full, rolling boil, time for one minute. It's never failed me.  

There are a few variations on this recipe, but this one is probably my favorite. I prefer the texture you get when you add the peanut butter after removing from heat as opposed to boiling it with the sugar, etc.  I also prefer the cocoa added in the beginning, but other good recipes call for it at the end.  Different strokes!

text:
This is an old familiar favorite of mine since childhood.  However, we called them Grandma's "Boiled Cookies," simply because she boiled them on the stovetop.

My Grandmother used the exact same ingredients and exact same amounts.  However, boiling time is crucial and essential.  We add the Peanut Butter with the other ingredients to boil (milk, butter/oleo, sugar, cocoa, salt) and bring the mixture to a hard boil over a medium flame(roughly, 4 - 5 minutes from beginning to boil).  We were too poor to afford a candy thermometer, I suppose.  THIS IS WHERE GRANDMA TOLD ME THAT THE TEXTURE PROBLEM LIES - " ... Too little boiling time, runny/wet & unable to set properly (because the mix did not reach high enough temperature to become the confection); while too much time produced dry & crumbly cookies (result of too hot too long, burning off moisture)."

Also, I choose to use Super Chunky peanut butter for more peanut texture and Grandma is probably rolling in her grave, but it defintely works for me!

Then, after we remove the boiling mixture from the flame and stir in the vanilla and quick oats (one-minute), spooning out mixture onto wax-paper lined cookie sheets.  Also, I've noticed that if I use baking/cooling racks, these tend to cool and set a little more rapidly.  So, if you're like me and can't wait ... 

I've never had a soft batch.  They're definitely one of my all-time favorites.  Not to mention the favorites of any guests and all of my neices and nephews!

text:
I have made these no-bakes many times successfully. I always boil for about 2 minutes (candy thermometer reads about 210-120 which is above jelly stage but below thread stage).  I find that I have enough time to drop all the cookies without them getting hard, but they will start to jell near the end.  Have ready a couple of cookie sheets lined with wax paper so that you can drop them all without any hardening.  Another tip: make sure peanut butter and oats are measured and ready to go once your timer goes off at 2 minutes. The final product is shiny and chewy but no where near gooey.  And yes, they are sweet, but they are so yummy!

I love these cookies, but I'm too lazy to use the stove so I microwave them instead.  Put everything but the oats, pb and vanilla in a bowl and cook for 3 1/2 minutes, stir and then cook for 3 1/2 more minutes and stir in the oats and stuff.  I've also done it once where I left out the cocoa and microwaved the rest but at the end I added oats and cut up peanut butter cups and they melted beautifully.

LOVE THE QUICKNESS!!  We opened a store 4 weeks ago & everyone has been asking for homemade cookies.  I tried these thinking no one would really buy them because they are so easy to make anyone can make them.  Guess Again!!  I have been making 4 batches of these a day & am still running out!! These are the easiest quickest HOT SELLING cookies I have ever made.  Thanks!!

text:
This is THE PERFECT no bake cookie recipe. It is a perfect balance of peanut butter and chocolate--you can taste them both, but neither overpower the other. It is CRUCIAL to follow the directions about timing 1 minutes after liquid comes to a full, rolling boil. If you are a new cook, that means when the entire surface of the liquid is covered with bubbles. It's also important to use a pot with a level bottom so that the entire mixture gets heated evenly. I have some older pots that are warped that I use for abusive dishes like mashed potatoes, but that kind cannot make good no bake cookies. Stir, stir, stir in the peanut butter quickly, add the oats, then spoon them out as quickly as possible. If you leave the cookie mix lingering in the hot pan they will become dry and hard, just as if you overcooked them. Sounds complicated, but once you figure it out, you will have the best no bake cookies on the block!

text:
I'm rating 2 stars because they left an essential part of the recipe out - YOU ARE TO STIR CONSTANTLY FROM BEGINNING TO END!!!  Omit the salt, up the Hershey's cocoa to 5 tbls. Once it starts to boil, boil for 2 minutes. CONSTANTLY stirring.  When 2 minutes are up, remove from heat and quickly add the peanut butter (off brands work better) 1 minute quick oats and vanilla. Stir well.  Drop onto waxed paper and let them set up in the refrigerator.  Also store in refrig. or cold pantry.  We've been making these since the 60's.  And they always come out great.  Another tip:  when they start to boil, turn down the heat just enough to keep it rapidly boiling.  Some people don't understand that the heat doesn't have to be kept on HIGH to keep it boiling.  Also, when starting to make, mix the sugar and cocoa well, get it wet with the milk, then add the stick of butter to the pan.  Stir till it starts to boil, put on timer for 2 minutes, keep stirring until timer goes off.  Quickly add the last 3 ingredients. Mix well and drop and don't stop.  If you would find the mixture is hardening before you are done dropping - return to stove, add a little milk, stir until it's wet again.  New cooks seem to have this problem.  UPDATE:  Don't boil 4-5 minutes.  This is BAD for the sugar content.  ALSO - measure the oats in a one cup meas. cup 3 times rather than your large 4 cup measuring cup.  It's more exact.  Have everything pre-measured and cookie sheets ready before you even start to cook.

Absolutely perfect!!!  I followed the recipe exactly, and it turned out perfect.  Took the advice from another review and waited until it reached a full rolling boil before starting the 1 minute timer.  Also, before boiling the other ingredients, I measured out the oats, then plopped the peanut butter on top of them, made a dent in the middle of the peanut butter & poured the vanilla in it.  This way it was easy to add all 3 of these ingredients immediately after removing the pan from the heat.  They turned out perfect - set up nicely, and were not too dry nor too gooey.  My husband wants me to make these every week now!

text:
I have been making a version of these cookies for over 50 years since my aunt Ida taught me how to make them when I was 8 years old. There are a couple of things that I suggest to make them easier and better. First, don't use margarine. These are far better with butter. Second, use 5 tablespoons of cocoa rather than 3. 

For ease of mixing, add the peanut butter when you take the boiling mixture off the heat. Completely mix it in before you add the vanilla. Adding vanilla immediately causes the alcohol in the vanilla to boil and evaporate and the flavor isn't as good. Finally, add the oats. 

I use parchment paper rather than wax paper and I don't use cookie sheets - I just lay the paper on the countertop.

These are a family favorite and one of the first cookies I taught my daughters to make. To the person who said the boiling time is not enough, I've been making these for over 40 years and have discovered that if the humidity is high/its raining, etc., yes you will have to boil the mixture longer. text:
First time i made them they were delicious, but they werre way to greasy for me to feel good about. This time I brought about 2 tbsp of butter, 1/2 c white sugar, 1/3 c agave, milk, cocoa, and salt to a rapid boil for 1min. Working quickly (having everything prepped in advance) I added the peanut butter to melt, then 1 small mashed banana, and once all incorporated, I added the vanilla and oats.  They turned out way less greasy, but equally delicious. The banana adds a subtle flavour, but its works well with the peanut butter and chocolate. I'm proud that I figured out an alternative that works!

text:
Despite conflicting reviews on whether the cookies will set or not following the given directions, I decided to follow the recipe to the "T".  I made sure the ingredients that are meant to come to a boil came to a full rolling boil while stirring.  At that point, I set a timer for 1 minute and continued stirring while the mixture boiled.  As soon as I put in the remaining ingredients, I knew the cookies were not going to set properly.  I went ahead and put them out on the waxed paper.  Usually, no bake cookies set fairly rapidly upon cooling, but these did not.  The kids couldn't wait any longer and were scooping the cookies up with a spoon and eating them.  By the next morning, about 12 hours later, they had set enough to at least be able to pick them up.  They were still a little more "wet" than most no bake cookies.  
Even though they took awhile to set, they still tasted fine.  In my opinion, the sticky ones are much better than coming out with dry, crumbly cookies.

text:
I love No-Bake cookies.  I love to cook and bake anything, and I'm very good at both.  However, for years I've tried to make these cookies, and I could never get it right - the ingredients would turn into a dry, crumbly non-formable mess.  It was so frustrating and disappointing ("was" being the operative word!!) Recently, I had a strong craving for them, and I knew I wanted to conquer this cookie!!  So with the help of a reviewer' comments and a friend's recommendation - I was able to be a accomplish my goal! A friend suggested, to overcome the dry crumbly mess I was getting to use a heaping measurement for the peanut butter - so I used a heaping 1/2 cup of peanut butter - maybe closer to 3/4 cup.  With the recommendation of a fellow reviewer of this recipe - I waited until the ingredients came to a full rolling boil before I began the 1-minute timer!  With those suggestions my cookies were perfect!  I will definitely be using this recipe again!

text:
These are a family favorite. We've been making them our whole lives. You don't have a family party without "Mess Cookies". The only problem is that the recipe has been a little muddled, passing verbally from one person to the next. No one could agree on the cooking times, so I started testing. The key to the no bake cookies is the boil time. You MUST have your mix at a hard boil (you stir and the boiling isn't reduced). Do not time before this point and only cook at a rolling boil for 1 minute. If you cook it at the wrong time, you will either get hard dry cookies or very gooey cookies that will NOT set up (thus our naming them Messy).   This recipe has all the portions correctly. It is excellent :D

None
text:
My recipe has a few differences: an extra cup sugar, an extra tbsp cocoa, an extra 1/2 cup butter, no salt, 4 tbsp p-butter instead of 1/2 cup (I think it's about the same amount though), & an extra tsp vanilla. My directions: mix sugar, cocoa, butter, milk & "bring to a ROLLING boil, & continue to boil for 1 minute. Add oats, peanut butter & vanilla, & beat until fairly thick. Remove from heat & drop by spoonfuls onto greased cookie sheets or waxed paper. Place in a cool dry place & let sit for at least 1 hour." In my experience making these, the following works best: 1) you need to bring the mixture to a good, rolling boil before timing - this cooking helps blend the flavor of the cocoa with the other ingredients & make it deep and rich; 2) you need to have the oats, peanut butter & vanilla measured out and ready to go as soon as you pull the mix off the stove; 3) use a large wooden spoon to stir the whole thing in the pan  youre literally going to "beat" the mixture by hand. It is very tiresome, but the longer you "beat", the thicker the mixture becomes, the less shine it has, & the better it will set once placed on your cookie sheet. BEWARE: It *is* possible to over-mix, & wind up with crumbly cookies. You want to beat the mixture until thick & it has lost some of its shine, not until it's chunky. Chunky means you've beaten too much (or taken too long and the mixture has cooled). These are very rich cookies, & not for the faint of heart.

text:
This recipe works well as is, but I make a bunch of modifications to suit my own tastes and needs. I like my cookies very fudgy and almost gooey; I want them to have more chocolate flavor but not lose the peanut butter and finally, I want them to pack a slightly healthier punch. So... if you don't want yours like that, you can move on to the next review, if you do, here's how I modify them.
1. decrease sugar by 1/3 cup.
2. decrease milk by a couple of tbs and use 2 pinches of sea salt.
3. increase peanut butter to a full cup.
4. use 9 tbsp of Hershey's Special Dark Cocoa instead of 3 of regular.
5. use real butter, it's healthier than margarine.
6. use old fashioned oats and add them right after the peanut butter, then add back in those 2 tbsp of milk to help soften them a bit (don't worry, it'll set because of the chocolate chips, keep reading.)
7. add 2 Tbsp Ground Golden Flax Seed with the oats.
8. add 1/3 c. of special dark chocolate chips.
9. after adding the peanut butter, oats, vanilla, flax seed, and chocolate chips, stir slowly over low heat until the chocolate chips are melted and then scoop out onto the wax paper.
For the nutritionally inclined chocoholic who wants a decadent dark chocolate treat that still has some redeeming qualities, these are SOOOOO yummy!

text:
Great recipe,  but the timing is off.   As a hint,  the humidity has an effect on how the cookies will "set up".   What I do is bring the mixture to a boil,  then rolling boil for 3 minutes if it IS humid,  and 2 minutes if it is NOT humid.    Also,  in the winter,  I will make this recipe without the oatmeal and pour in a pan and let it set and cut into squares. This recipe has been around for 40 years or more!

text:
The ingredient ratio is perfect. The steps can use some work. First put your vanilla in with the oats mix then add your peanutbutter in with the oats, mix and set aside. The trick is to slowly heat the sauce. Start the heat on 3 and gradually work your way up to 4 and then 5 (med heat) till you get it to a rolling boil. You only need to boil it for one minute. My cookies come out perfect everytime.

All in all, the flavor was really good.

I grew up on these! Absolutely delicious! I also let it come to a FULL BOIL THEN start the timing -(1 to 2 mins) It's almost like candy so it needs to hit the right temp to 'set' correctly. (don't overcook or they will be too crumbly. 

I like to use extra crunchy peanut butter and a little less coco, but my kids perfer creamy and lots of coco - we've even added raisins for a nice change. The coconut idea sounds like something we will have to try. A word of warning for those of you in rainy areas... since it is a little like candy, the rainy days are not good days to make these (we have made some on rainy days and they are a little gooie and don't set right).

text:
My husband loves no bake cookies - I used to buy them at Wal-Mart for him.  I finally decided to make my own and found this recipe.  He told me he likes these better than the store bought cookies!  I read through hundreds of reviews and followed a few tips from other people, and these have turned out great every time.  I did try reducing the sugar, per some reviews, but my husband and kids like them sweeter.  I wait for the full boil, then start timing.  I have found that it takes a little longer than the minute, maybe 15-20 seconds longer, probably has something to do with high altitude.  I put the peanut butter on top of the oats and pour the vanilla on top of that, so that everything is ready to mix in when the boiling is done.  I always have my husband help drop them onto the pans and have never had trouble getting them dropped before it hardens.  He also cleans up all the drips :)  Thanks for the recipe, and all the helpful reviews!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I have been making these for years and years. Always perfect and delicious. Make sure you are using real butter or real margarine. It must have 100 calories per tablespoon to be real. Anything else is a margarine spread (even if it is in stick form) and should never be used in a recipe. It will not allow your cookies or candy to set up or harden. If your cookies did not set up, this may be the cause. Another cause may be not allowing mixture to come to a full rolling boil. A full rolling boil is a boil that can't be stirred down. 1 minute cooking time (after it has reached the full boil stage) allows a creaminess to the cookie texture that you won't get if you boil it too long.

text:
This is a great no bake cookie recipe. I added 4 Tablespoons of cocoa instead of 3, and an extra 1/2 cup of oats. Make sure you boil the mixture for the full 1 minute. I actually boiled it for over a minute and it came out wonderful. Just make sure you hit the 1 minute mark. A little over won't kill this recipe, but a little under could. I also poured the whole thing onto a cookiesheet lined with wax paper and pressed it out flat, then took a cookie cutter after it cooled to get fun shapes instead of the "drops" of cookies you usually see. Thanks for this awesome recipe!

Make it like the recipe says, don't change half the ingredients and still expect them to be good. Don't forget to use parchment paper though! :)

country:
None
text:
I have made this recipe too many times to count and they've always received rave reviews. Personally, I think they're "just ok" but almost everyone I serve them to seems to love them. And because the cookies are very easy to make and don't require turning on the oven, this recipe gets 5 stars. I've tried a variety of changes including decreasing the sugar (you really don't need 2 cups), slightly decreasing the butter (which I use instead of margarine), slightly increasing the peanut butter. I've adjusted batch size (increased and decreased) to good effect. But if you want to double the recipe you should note that it'll take longer to drop all the cookies and the mixture may start to set in the saucepan. When this happens to me, I just put the saucepan over high heat for just a few seconds. Also note - do NOT substitute veg oil in whole or part for the margarine.. this will not work well and the cookies will be crumbly (though still tasty).

These are the same ingredients in the recipe my mom used(and now I use), except hers called for only 1 T. peanut butter. Also, to get better consistency, bring them to a full boil over medium heat stirring constantly and continue boiling for 2 minutes. I don't think they're quite as good if you boil them too rapidly - don't set up as well. But a huge hit! These are excellent - just experiment a bit to get the right heat and timing. Also, I prefer less peanut butter than 1/2 C.  Think my mom's recipe of 1 T. is about right.

text:
My baby daughter has a dairy, egg, nut allergies.  A friend of mine had introduced this receipe to me without the peanut butter and using soymilk. We were thrilled it set up.  It was my first time eating chocolate in six months.  I have since played with the receipe.  I have substituted the milk with vanilla soymilk (no need for adding more vanilla,)dairy free margarine in place of butter, baker's sugar because boiling time is much shorter and so is stir time and I use Sunbutter instead of peanut butter.  I have added 1/4 cup sunflower seeds also at the end and it really makes the cookie that much better.  I hope someone else with children with food allergies will benefit from me sharing my tweeking of this excellent receipe.

Thanks for a great recipe.  I think it is important to do the following:  Fill your sink up with hot, soapy water first.  Prepare all of your ingredients to have at hand in front of you, including laying out the wax paper.  Once the mixture comes to a full rolling boil, then time it one minute.  I mixed it around once about every 10 seconds.  After the minute, pour in the next ingredients and mix them together half way on the burner and then continue by removing it from the heat.  Work really quickly scooping it out, doesn't matter how they look.  Put your pot along with all those measuring things you used to have at hand in the hot soapy water for an easy cleanup!

So for a first timer making these, I had to try it two times to get them right.
First time I did the way it was directed and eh. Second time I went with the changes of 1.5 cups of sugar and boiling for two minutes, and they are not kidding guys- you gotta move with lightning fast speed otherwise those suckers dull up and turn into a crumbling mess (first time I was thinking, Ive got a little time, 30 seconds wont mess it up that bad) and I was so, so wrong. . Get everything prepped before hand and stir everything up like a middle aged woman named Karen running late is watching you make her latte! Stir the entire time and dump em on the wax paper as quick as you can. And then behold your beautiful creations!

text:
These are awesome but I add a little more cocoa than the recipe calls for. They are devoured at family gatherings and are always requested to be made year round from family. I do boil mine longer than the one minute it calls for. A great way to check them to see if they are done is the old school trick you do with fudge, by dropping a tiny amount of the liquid into cold water. If it splatters, that means it needs to cook longer but if it turns into a "ball", it is done. Easy, yummy cookies.

text:
I love this recipe! It worked perfectly this time. Shiny, soft and tasty. Didn't change a thing...used real butter, 2% milk and Skippy peanut butter. In my experience, the weather, the type of peanut butter and butter really can make the difference. I stir constantly until the rolling boil, that can't be stirred down. The time can change between 1-2 minutes, watch the texture on the spoon. Then put a lid on the mixture for that minute without stirring. If heat is high you could burn the mixture. The moisture from the lid keeps sugar crystals from forming which makes the cookie dry and gritty...The lid hint came from Alton Brown making fudge. Works for me...

text:
i have made these all of my life...i assemble them a bit differently...i mix milk, sugar, cocoa,butter, then bring to boil for 1 solid min maybe a few extra seconds...i judge it by the look when it starts to look glossy its perfect ...if you cook too long you get cookies that are brittle, not long enough soggy...so if you stir the whole time then when you cant stir away the bubbles then time for 1 min turn off heat add peanut butter let melt and vanilla...then i add a bit less oatmeal as 3 cups makes them too thick and not creamy enough try adding like 2 1/2 cups maybe a bit more ..if you play with this a bit you will be pleased...but please 2 min is too long to boil...like i said i have made these my entire life its always been 1 min after it comes to rapid boil that is the trick...and stir constantly...you will have better results good luck

Yum! perfect recipe, thanks Robin!

Just a couple changes to keep cookies from getting crumbly:

add peanut butter thats room temperature, or microwave it before adding. Cook sauce just a lil after adding peanut butter. add about 1/4 less oats than written. Also, use old fashioned oats instead of quick cooking oats for a better texture.

I was craving chocolate and all we had was cocoa powder, so I found this.  I halved the butter, cut out a 1/2 cup of sugar, and added a tbsp of cocoa.  Definitely have the oats, peanut butter, and vanilla all in a bowl and ready to dump into the boiling ingredients together- it wouldn't have worked well otherwise.I think it would taste better with natural peanut butter, since it's still very sugary, so maybe I'll try that next time.  It's a great quick fix if you lack ingredients and don't feel like running to the store.

text:
I have always loved these cookies since my grandmother used to make them when I was a child.  If you think about it, it's essentially a fudge recipe with oats added in.  My grandmother used to add coconut as well as oats, which is a nice variation.  I like a heartier oat presence (and chewiness) and so I use half quick cooking, and half old-fashioned oats.  I have also increased the total amount of oats at times, which is a different way to make a less sweet, healthier cookie, and I find they turn out fine that way too.

Excellent no-bake recipe! This is one that it always requested in my house for the holidays and they always disappear before they cool. This EXACT recipe always turns out perfectly and I have made it dozens of times. Allowing the mixture to boil rapidly for exactly one minute is crucial. They are runny at first but set up beautifully. Make them small and don't bother trying to double the recipe. It will be crumbly by the time you form all the cookies.

text:
These cookies are delicious! I did follow the recipe exactly for measurements and such but with only one exception. I read a handful of reviews prior to starting and decided to take the advice of boiling the mixture just a bit longer. One minute of rapid boiling isn't long enough for the sugar to transition from just being wet and sticky to becoming a combining agent. I waited until my cocoa mixture came to a complete rapid boil and started timing then, for 2 minutes 15 seconds and the cookies turned out perfectly. Otherwise a SUPER easy and amazingly delicious recipe! Thank you! :)

text:
The secret is to boil the mixture for 4-6 min... the longer you boil the more the sugar carmelizes and the quicker the cookies will set up once you remove them from the heat. If they look a little watery (like my first batch did) then just let the mixture set for a few min before spooning them out on the wax paper. These are so delicious!!! I've made them several times. With and without peanut butter... you can add almost anything to these cookies. I've even made coffee almond ones! I also use dark chocolate cocoa and it makes them even more decadent. I will continue to make these for a loooong time!

Follow this trick for a perfect no bake cookie- bring to a rolling boil over medium heat for 90 seconds and DO NOT STIR, if you stir these or boil them over high heat they turn out DRY, if you don't bring them to a rolling boil or don't cook them for 90 seconds then turn out too SOFT and do not set! You will end up with a perfect cookie guaranteed!!

text:
I've been making these for years but I think there are two keys to making these.  One is to make sure the mixture is at a FULL BOIL for 1 full minute (I do not like the consistency when I boil them longer).  And the other thing is not to make them on rainy days because it's been my experience that they don't set up right if there's too much humidity in the air.  My family loves these cookies, and it's nice for me that they are so easy and quick to make.

I'd just like to add that the freshness of the peanut butter you use really makes a difference; if your peanut butter is not fresh enough it may taste as though you made a mistake in your preparation when you didn't. Also, try adding just a little bit (a couple teaspoons) of caramel. One more thing, sometimes I use chocolate rice crispies like cereal instead of oatmeal (you might think that the no bakes have enough chocolate in them already and the extra chocolate wont taste so good but believe me you got to try it). I commonly use 'Malt-O-Meal Cocoa Dyno-Bites' which comes in bags instead of boxes like normal cereal and it works great.

text:
Classic no-bake recipe.  Excellent!  I boiled the mixture for 3-3.5 minutes and that was a tad too long (the cookies were a bit crumbly).

Probably, 2-2.5 minutes is right around right.  I have noticed several reviewers saying that their cookies wouldn't set up correctly and 1 minute (as the recipe says) is probably not enough.  If your cookies don't set up it's most likely because the mixture didn't get hot enough (whereas if it's crumbly or a bit dry, it was boiled a bit too long).

Also, beware of sugar subs for this type of recipe because they can do unexpected things (I know for a fact that granulated fructose simply won't work with this recipe).

text:
I started making this recipe about a month ago and have since made over ten batches for different people/functions.  They take about ten minutes to make including the time to get all the ingredients from the cabinet.  

I quickly divide up the items to be boiled and separate them from the items to be added (pb, vanilla and oats) so they can be added quickly after removing from heat.  I then lay out a sheet of wax paper and then get to work.  So easy!

Boiling seems to be about 2 1/2 minutes to get just right.  This is with adding 3/4 cup crunchy peanut butter (the peanuts are awesome in there!), 1/3 cup coconut (even better texture!) and 1/2 cup less sugar (have to do something about that 170 calories per cookie.. hehe).

YUMMY!! FUN!! AND EASY TO MAKE!! These are great tasting cookies.  Very sweet. I used some of the suggestions from previous reviews i.e. I used rolled oats/old fashioned oats(21/2 cups) and raw organic sugar.  I also boiled it for 2-full min. However I believe that 1 1/2 min would also do the trick and allow you a little more time to place the cookies on the wax paper before they set.  I also made a batch using crunchy peanut butter.  I found those not to be as creamy as the ones I made with the smooth peanut butter. As stated earlier these cookies are yummy my whole family loved them. TRY THEM AND ENJOY!!!!!  OH... I almost forgot I also used organic CAROB POWDER...you'll never miss the chocolate(I promise).

text:
I've been making this recipe for years with only a few minor changes that make this easy recipie even easier.  I only use 1 stick butter and I use 4T cocoa.  I put the milk and butter in a glass bowl, and microwave for 1 min.  Add salt, cocoa and sugar and microwave for 5 min, stiring occasionally.  Add vanilla and p-nut butter, blend well, add oats and stir.  Drop by spoonfuls onto wax paper and throw in the fridge.  I love that I always have all of the ingriedents on hand, and if I am having a real chocolage craving I will put the first tray in the freezer.

text:
I love this recipe. I have been making these cookies with my kids for over 25 years. This is the first cookie I made with the kids. They are now 27 and 22 and still ask for them. I have never had problems with the cookies turning out to crumbly or gooey. I have always waited until the mixture has come to a full rolling boil then start my timer for 2 minutes. I believe that if your cookies are not setting then you started your timer to early. Your mixture has to be at a full rolling boil before you set your timer.

text:
Excellent no-bakes!! I previosly had a recipe that called for 2 cups quick-cooking oats and boiled hard for 3 minutes, and those cookies did not work at all - they were always flat, gooey puddles. So I definitely recommend boiling for 1-2 minutes and using 3 cups quick-cooking oats. Also, with this recipes, I added about 1/2 cup of grape nuts (for an added crunch and nutritional benefit), which tasted delicious. :) Highly recommended!

text:
These cookies were a staple item growing up in the South. Although most of the same recipes call for the same ingredients, the key to this one being the best, in my opinion, is that the author made sure to mention working quickly! If you dont start spooning them out as soon as you get the mixture completely combined, they wont set up and will stay tacky. Take the author and my word for it, work quickly to get them on the wax paper! They will begin to set up almost immediately.

text:
Great recipe to follow! Instead of cooling my cookies on parchment paper, I actually like a rectangle cake pan with parchment paper then spray it with Pam cooking spray. Once that's done, I poor my peanut butter no bake recipe straight into the pan. I let that cool in the fridge & sort of set while I make my chocolate no bakes. Once the chocolate recipe is all done, I poor it over the peanut butter no bake. Again I place the pan in the fridge to cool & set. Cool for  about an hour, cut & serve. The end result is a Reeces Cup no bake bar! This is a little time consuming but easy & absolutely delicious!! I hope y'all try this. Enjoy!
Boo Boo

Display Name:
Victoria Irvin

https://images.media-allrecipes.com/userphotos/50x50/2866119.jpg
city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
I first tried these when I was at a potluck in Florida. The guy who brought them said his mom makes them all the time. I think I ate about 80% of what he brought!! No shame here. :) 

Some notes from my learning that hailed from disasters:

- I live at a high altitude in a very dry area. You may have to adjust your recipe. I had to adjust boiling time and milk. Don't be afraid to experiment. 

- Use a big enough pot to do this or you will have a big mess to clean up and none of it will be edible. 

- Use unsalted butter instead of margarine. I've found margarine doesn't seem to let the cookies set up. Don't get me wrong. They are still edible (the cook gets the edible mistakes, right?). 

- Please wait until you have boiled the candy and taken the pot off the heat before you add the vanilla as it evaporates pretty fast so wait so it gives the cookies just another layer of flavor.

- If you want a really easy way to get these cookies out onto the wax paper quick, use a little disher, like the ones for ice cream. Inside on the sweeper is a number that tells you what size it is. Get yourself a disher that has the number 100 on it. Perfect size and makes the job way faster. Also, these are really not going to spread much so there is no need to leave a lot of room between each cookie. 

- Lastly... if you really want these to last until the family gets home, you get to that event, or you make it to your friend's birthday, do what I do...make another batch!

text:
I had a few friends over for a dinner party and one of the ladies is allergic to eggs.  I was looking for a quick desert that didn't require eggs and found this recipe.
I remember making these when I was a kid and liked them, so for me this was perfect.
I didn't think there was enough cocoa powder so I used an extra 1/2 T and it was just right.
I did what another reviewer suggested and timed my rapid boil for 2 min.  It was a mistake.  They tasted really good, but came out a little too crumbly.  They held their shape when I scooped them out and put them on waxed paper, but after cooling completely when you bit into them the texture was just a little too dry.
Next time I make these I will time my rapid boil for 1 min., as the recipe instructs.
I didn't think these were too sweet, they were just right, it balanced out the richness of the cocoa powder and the peanut butter.

Delicious & so easy!! I took these to a cookie exchange & they nicknamed them "crack cookies." Lol... I did follow some of the siggestions from the other reviews. I melt the peanut butter with everything else in the sauce pan. I also bring to a ROLLING boil & then set timer for 2 minutes stirring frequently. After I add quick oats I let it stand for 1 minute before dropping onto wax paper. Perfect texture & flavor for us. Thank you!! I will be making these again!

text:
This was a good start if you are willing to change and experiment a little. I used the other review suggestions of 
-1 1/2 cups sugar
-natural peanut butter
To specify the boiling... 
-1 minute is not long enough! I tried 1min 10 sec. The first day and they were very messy and gooey still. 
-The next day I boiled 1 min 40 sec., and it took the cookies 4-5 hours to finally set up 
-I WOULD SUGGEST TIMING YOUR BOILING FOR 2 MINUTES FROM THE ONSET OF BOILING POINT.

text:
This is a favorite in my community.  I live in Guatemala, and many people do not have ovens.  So every time I make these wonderful little morsels, I am besieged for a lesson to make them.  Normally I just make them following the recipe (except I always use butter, not margarine, or coconut oil), but we do love them with added cinnamon (we like it a lot, but you decide what you like) and/or coconut.  I normally just pour the hot cookies into a cake pan and cut when cool.  They stay softer longer, although they never seem to be around long enough to dry out.  They take no time to make and the ingredients are fairly common to find here.

Rolling boil for one whole minute is the best advice. Not just a few bubbles, an actual rolling boil for one whole minute. This recipe is as old as the hills.  My mom had a large family to feed so she doubled the recipe.  4 c. sugar, 8TBS cocoa 2 sticks real butter, 1 c. milk, 2tsp. vanilla, 1c. peanut butter 6 c. oats.  I put mine in an 11 by 7 inch pan.  I don't think they're as crumbly that way.  They are sweet but who cares.  If you double it like I do, simply remove 1/2 c. of oats from smaller oat container and use the rest.

text:
These tasted great. They weren't as smooth and creamy as I would have liked but I followed the advice of others and started my one  minute timer once the mixture came to a rolling boil. They seemed a tad overcooked, a smidge on the dry side. No bakes are a tricky cookie to make - a little overcooked can make a dry cookie. I also used butter instead of margarine (I never buy margarine) and it worked great.  I used my large cookie scoop (#24) and it made 18 perfect size cookies. Work fast though, the "batter" got stiff the longer it stayed in the pan.

text:
I have made a few different no bake recipes, all of which have pretty much the same ingredients at different quantity. I find this one to be just about right for me. The only change I made was margarine to butter. I have tried both and there is a difference in taste and texture. 
I do want to share a tip that took me some time to figure out. Almost all of the recipes that I have seen tell you to boil for a set time, usually between 1 and 2 minutes. I could never get the texture I wanted until I finally googled the trick/science behind the perfect no bake cookie. The key to texture is in the boiling. You have to get it to the soft ball stage on a candy thermometer. It actually took me almost 3 minutes to achieve this temp. And after about the two minute mark I was getting a little nervous but stuck to my guns and let it reach the required temp. 
I am so glad that I did. My cookies turn out perfect every single time now. I actually don't even use the thermometer anymore. I've timed it a few times and now know that it takes about 3 minutes for me. Now maybe I am cooking at a lower temp or something but 3 minutes is what it takes at medium heat on my stove. Of course the time will differ with everybody depending on many variables im sure. 
Anyone having texture issues should try this method. Also, one chef suggested not stirring once it starts to boil. I also follow that rule. As soon as it reaches temp I take off of heat and I immediately stir in vanilla and peanut butter. Make

text:
I made these again tonight for about the hundreth time, at least that's what it feels like. Everyone loves these cookies and I get requests for them over and over.  I always start my 1 minute timing AFTER the mixture reaches a full, rolling boil.  I make the entire recipe in one saucepan on the stove - love the easy cleanup!!  Two things I've learned - you can sub butter for the margarine and half-n-half for the milk (which I did tonight in a pinch); and the longer you stir the mixture after you add the oatmeal, the uglier they become.  Stir JUST UNTIL mixed and they will retain a lovely gloss. I've tried other recipes and this is my favorite!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
The first time I made these I used all natural peanut butter NOT kept in the fridge (which can be pretty liquidy), and subbed 1 cup of honey for all the sugar. They pretty runny even though I added 1 extra cup of oats, but after putting them in the freezer for 30min and then storing them in the fridge, they set fine. This time I made the recipe for 36 instead of 24, still subbing the half portion of honey but using regular peanut butter and no extra oats, and they got much thicker much quicker! I had to race to get them spooned out before they got so dry they wouldn't stick together! But the best thing was that I used my MUFFIN PANS and smushed a large spoonful down into each cup (no liners or oil or anything), stuck them in the freezer again (30min), and when I took them out I could pry out each perfectly shaped cookie with a butter knife and they didn't crumble or break! I will use less peanut butter next time (or go back to the thinner, natural kind), but I just love these cookies! I'm going to try using olive oil instead of butter and almond milk instead of regular one time, and then they will be GF AND DF (not that I care but other people do haha).

Back home people used to make these no back cookies for just about everything, here at college it was like no one had ever heard of them.... Instead, I lined a muffin tin with cupcake papers, dropped just enough mini chocolate chips in the bottom to cover, patted the warm mix in, then sprinkled a few more mini chips on top.  Refrigerated for awhile just to set the chocolate, then brought back up to room temp.

None
text:
We've been making no-bake cookies for years and many of the reviewers are right about waiting for a FULL roiling boil before starting the timer, though we're in the military and we move around a lot, so we've found that if you live in a humid climate, you have to boil the cookies for longer and in dry climates, you don't.  One minute works fine in dry climates and much more humid climates require up to a minute and a half.  If you're trying these for the first time, make a guess on the time (1 min for desert, 1:30 for the tropics, gauge if you're somewhere in between!)  I would recommend cooking it a few seconds longer than you think you need to, I'd rather have slightly crumbly cookies than ones that don't set up!  Good luck!

text:
These are incredible!  I changed servings to 36  (which actually made 50 cookies) to accommodate daughter's choir party. I also added the peanut butter before boiling and boiled 2 minutes--SMOOOOTH!!!  I've had grainy ones before (not enough cook time=undissolved sugar). Also, didn't have to work terribly quickly at dropping onto baking sheet, in fact, took about 15 minutes to get all cookies on sheet, and the further I got along, the cooler the batter was and actually held itself up rather than spreading as the earlier, hotter batter did. Thanks, Robin, for a fantastic recipe, and to all other reviews!

text:
This recipe is the one like my childhood recipe. We call it cookie crack..it's so addictive. Anyway. I tried one minute after rolling boil. Set up but took a long time, overnight really, but half were gone by then anyway. Second time I cooked 4 min from first boil. I watched when the full rolling boil started at this ended up being 2.5 min after rolling boil. And stirred CONSTANTLY.(I also added 1/2 cup more oats for 3.5 cups total) This batch set up in 15 min and my family preferred the texture. I personally would cut cooking back by 1/2 min so 2 min after rolling boil or 3.5 min from first boil, and stir not so much. Hope this helps.

I made these cookies the other day for my step-son. I read many of the reviews before I made them. I did change the margarine to butter and added 1/2 cup of oats (for a total of 3 1/2 cups) per suggestions. I would like to add more cocoa powder next time. The cookies firmed up just great and my step-son and husband ate them all up !! Thanks for sharing the recipe !!

text:
These aren't the same as what my mom made, but with a few changes they get close. My mom never used peanut butter, so I made a few changes. I substituted the PB for extra cocoa in the initial boil as well as reduced the amount of sugar. The trick is to wait for a real rapid boil to start your timer for one minute. Then I added my oats ( I only had the old fashioned kind, so I had to let them cook in the mixture for a minute or two) and about a 1/4 cup of chocolate chips. Mine didn't need wax paper, I just  plopped them on a plate and stuck them in the fridge while I made dinner. Never really formed perfectly, but they are still a little taste of heaven. MMMM

text:
After reading some reviews, I did two things to make sure the cookies would not be too runny.  First, I added the sauce to the oatmeal so I could see if I needed all the sauce or not.  Second, a friend told me to let the cookie mixture sit in the bowl a little bit to cool down and then spoon it on wax paper.  This worked great.  For a creamier taste, you can also add marshmellows with the peanut butter and stir until all is melted.  Great recipe!

Ok everyone listen up!  I have NEVER never been able to get my no bake cookies to set up right, until now!  I promise you this recipe works.  I have tried over a dozen recipes and none of them have worked.  You would not believe how excited I was when I got off of work to come home to perfectly set up cookies.  They peeled right off of the parchment paper like they should.  I always hate when people review a recipe and say they changed this or that. But I have to be one of those people too.  I added about 1/2-1 cup more of oats and boiled the sugar, cocoa, milk, and butter for about 5 minutes.  I was scared it wouldn't set up and so I just had to change a few things.  Next time though I am going to cook them as the recipe says and I'll let you know how they turned out then!  Be sure to try this recipe!!! It works!!!

text:
This is the very first time I ever made these cookies and they were simply wonderful - thanks not only to this great recipe but also to some of the wonderful tips found among the reviews.  For me some key things were to be sure to have everything prepared peanut butter, oats and vanilla so they are ready to add at the right time and also have ready the 'wax' paper.  I actually didn't have any wax paper so I used, successfully, both plastic coated freezer and the new Reynolds Wrap Release (non stick)aluminum foil.  I tried both just in case one didn't work but they both worked great.  Thanks to all!

This has always been my ALL TIME FAVORITE cookie!!!  I've eaten enough to know!!  The most difficult thing about making these cookies is timing the boil just right.  If you boil too long, the dough will turn to crumbs.  If you don't boil long enough, the dough will not harden.  Either way, the dough still tastes great, though!! :)  ENJOY!!!
